They return distilled findings or implementation summaries with relevant paths, symbols, commands, reproduction evidence, and confidenceβÄînot unfiltered command logs.\n+\n+## Concurrency policy\n+\n+- Launch all ready independent lanes together; do not wait for one independent lane before starting another.\n+- Prefer several meaningful workstreams to dozens of microscopic agents. Adjust concurrency to the dependency graph, resource capacity, and conflict risk; no fixed agent count applies.\n+- Reuse coordinator discovery. Bound each lane to its own evidence or ownership area instead of making every worker scan the whole repository.\n+- Avoid redundant searches, duplicated expensive operations, and artificial lanes created only to raise agent count.\n+- Add lanes dynamically when new independent work appears. Collapse or cancel lanes that become redundant, and preserve useful partial results.\n+\n+## Read-heavy workflow policy\n+\n+Audits, reviews, discovery, research, mapping, and diagnostics default to parallel read-only specialist lanes divided by subsystem, concern, library, package, route group, risk category, or evidence source. Exactly one agent may write a file at a time.\n+- Use separate Codex worktrees for independent implementation chats or lanes when supported and appropriate. Otherwise declare strict path ownership before editing.\n+- Designate one integration owner for shared files. Use an explicit handoff before ownership moves between agents.\n+- Each implementation lane runs focused checks for its bounded work; centralized integration validation follows combination.\n+- Never casually merge over, overwrite, stage, or discard another lane's or the user's changes.\n+\n+## Runtime and expensive-resource ownership\n+\n+Assign one authoritative owner for each shared or expensive resource: the development server, port `3000`, shared browser sessions, databases, migration execution, full end-to-end suites, full production builds, dependency installation, manifests and lockfiles, generated assets, deployment environments, and the final synchronization workflow.\n+\n+Other lanes may consume existing logs or results and request targeted checks from the owner. Subagents absorb noisy searches, logs, stack traces, and repetitive evidence gathering, then return compact structured summaries. Store or reference large raw output instead of repeatedly pasting it. Summarization must not drop user requirements, unknowns, decisions, blockers, or unreviewed results.\n+\n+## Failure and recovery\n+\n+If one lane fails, independent lanes continue. The failed lane returns partial evidence and its blocker; the coordinator preserves completed work and may retry, narrow, split, reassign, or serialize only the affected portion. When a task requires a durable authored plan or implementation record, store that task-specific artifact under `Development_Docs` in accordance with its rules. A plan may otherwise remain in the task's coordination state or in the user-requested artifact.\n+\n+## When an execution plan is required\n+\n+Use this planning structure for work that is any of the following:\n+\n+- multi-step, cross-cutting, ambiguous, long-running, repository-wide, or high-risk;\n+- spread across multiple subsystems or suitable for multiple subagents;\n+- dependent on staged validation or likely to modify shared infrastructure;\n+- an audit, feature, refactor, bug investigation, test initiative, documentation effort, architecture change, data migration, deployment preparation, performance effort, accessibility effort, or cross-system project; or\n+- large enough that context loss, duplicated work, ownership ambiguity, or accidental restart is plausible.\n+\n+A trivial localized task may use a lightweight inline plan, but it must still respect ownership, repository safety, and finalization requirements.\n+\n+## Planning principles\n+\n+An execution plan must:\n+\n+- be self-contained enough for another coordinator to continue without rediscovering the task;\n+- preserve the exact user goal, terminology, constraints, acceptance criteria, methodology, and output format;\n+- separate requirements and invariants from implementation choices;\n+- identify verified facts, assumptions, unknowns, and canonical sources;\n+- represent work as a dependency graph rather than a falsely linear checklist;\n+- maximize safe, useful concurrency while identifying conflict-prone and serialized work;\n+- establish one coordinator, clear lane ownership, and one writer per file at a time;\n+- identify shared runtime and expensive resources with authoritative owners;\n+- define evidence, focused validation, integration validation, and completion criteria before implementation;\n+- remain updateable as discoveries change scope, dependencies, ownership, risk, or validation;\n+- record significant decisions and discoveries without exposing private chain-of-thought; and\n+- preserve completed work when the plan changes.\n+\n+## Required execution-plan template\n+\n+Use the following sections. βÄ€Not applicableβÄù is acceptable only with a short reason.\n+\n+### 1. Task identity\n+\n+```text\n+Task title:\n+Date:\n+Coordinator:\n+Repository and root:\n+Current branch/worktree and commit:\n+Governing documents:\n+Related issue, phase, audit, or feature:\n+Current task instructions:\n+Plan location/status:\n+```\n+\n+Copy or faithfully summarize the controlling task instructions. Link to the full source when a summary could lose detail.\n+\n+### 2. Objective\n+\n+Record:\n+\n+- desired end state;\n+- user-visible outcome;\n+- technical outcome; and\n+- why the work is being done.\n+\n+Use outcome language. Do not describe activity alone as success.\n+\n+### 3. Scope\n+\n+Record:\n+\n+- included work;\n+- explicit exclusions;\n+- areas and behaviors that must remain unchanged;\n+- existing completed or uncommitted work that must be preserved; and\n+- actions that require separate user authority.\n+\n+Parallelization never broadens this scope.\n+\n+### 4. Sources of truth\n+\n+List, in priority order:\n+\n+- current user instructions;\n+- governing specifications and approved `Development_Docs` material;\n+- maintained architecture, security, testing, and operational documentation;\n+- canonical code and data directories;\n+- relevant tests and runtime evidence;\n+- external dependencies or authoritative external documentation; and\n+- the rule to apply when sources disagree.\n+\n+State which facts were verified in the current task and which were inherited or require confirmation.\n+\n+### 5. Repository reality check\n+\n+Before delegation or modification, capture:\n+\n+```text\n+Git repository root:\n+Canonical remote/repository:\n+Active application:\n+Active branch and HEAD:\n+Upstream and ahead/behind/diverged state:\n+Complete working-tree classification:\n+Canonical startup command:\n+Required application port:\n+Relevant focused and full validation commands:\n+Generated, archived, obsolete, or excluded trees:\n+Existing uncommitted work and owner/provenance if known:\n+Safe synchronization action taken or deferred:\n+```\n+\n+For this repository, verify rather than assume the current baseline. The expected canonical shape is one root Next.js application on `main`, normal startup through `npm run dev:full`, and normal development port `3000`. If reality differs, stop treating the expectation as fact and update the plan.\n+\n+Do not inspect secrets, overwrite local databases, or treat generated validation copies as source. Classify unrelated and pre-existing work before editing.\n+\n+### 6. Assumptions and unknowns\n+\n+Use this table:\n+\n+| ID | Assumption or unknown | Impact if wrong | Verification method | Responsible lane | Can work proceed first? | Status/evidence |\n+| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n+| A1 |  |  |  |  | Yes/No |  |\n+\n+Do not silently convert an unknown into a requirement or conclusion.\n+\n+### 7. Parallelization assessment\n+\n+Answer explicitly:\n+\n+- Which work is meaningfully independent?\n+- Which work depends on another result?\n+- Which lanes can begin immediately?\n+- Which steps must be serialized, and for what concrete reason?\n+- Which resources are shared or exclusive?\n+- Which files or interfaces are conflict-prone?\n+- Which work should be read-only?\n+- Which write lanes need isolated worktrees?\n+- What is the maximum safe and useful concurrency under current capacity?\n+- Why does the chosen decomposition improve speed, coverage, reliability, or context management without redundant work?\n+- What conditions would cause a lane to be split, collapsed, cancelled, or serialized?\n+\n+For a substantial task that remains primarily sequential, document the dependency, safety, exclusive-resource, or overlapping-file reason. Ease of coordination is not enough.\n+\n+### 8. Dependency graph\n+\n+Represent lane identifiers, prerequisites, fan-out, fan-in, the critical path, and failure independence. A compact text or Mermaid graph is acceptable. For example:\n+\n+```text\n+P0 repository preflight\n+βî€βîÄβîÄ R1 read-only subsystem inventory βîÄβîê\n+βî€βîÄβîÄ R2 read-only test/risk inventory βîÄβîΦβîÄβîÄ I1 coordinator reconciliation\n+βîîβîÄβîÄ R3 read-only requirements review βîÄβî‰\n+                                      βî€βîÄβîÄ W1 isolated implementation lane βîÄβîê\n+                                      βîîβîÄβîÄ W2 isolated implementation lane βîÄβîΦβîÄβîÄ I2 shared-file integration\n+                                                                          βîîβîÄβîÄ V1 integrated validation\n+                                                                              βîîβîÄβîÄ F1 finalization\n+```\n+\n+Annotate:\n+\n+- prerequisites and blocking relationships;\n+- ready work and fan-out points;\n+- integration/fan-in points;\n+- the critical path;\n+- serialized shared-resource operations; and\n+- lanes that can continue if another lane fails.\n+\n+Do not force parallel work into a fake sequential checklist.\n+\n+### 9. Workstream matrix\n+\n+| Lane ID | Lane name | Objective | Agent role | Read/write | Owned scope | Owned paths | Explicit non-scope | Dependencies | Shared resources | Deliverables | Required evidence | Focused validation | Status | Blockers |\n+| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n+| R1 |  |  |  | Read-only |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | Ready |  |\n+\n+Every lane must have a non-overlapping evidence or edit boundary. If two write lanes need the same file, change the ownership or serialize the handoff before either edits.\n+\n+### 10. Subagent briefing template\n+\n+Use a bounded briefing such as:\n+\n+```text\n+Objective:\n+Background and governing requirements:\n+Scope:\n+Explicit non-scope:\n+Authorization: read-only | write\n+Owned concerns/paths:\n+Resources and paths you must not modify:\n+Dependencies and prerequisite evidence:\n+Constraints and invariants:\n+Required repository-wide searches or checks:\n+Required deliverable:\n+Required evidence (paths, symbols, commands, reproduction, confidence):\n+Focused validation:\n+Return format (compact summary, changes, evidence, tests, blockers):\n+Completion criteria:\n+Stop conditions:\n+Blocker/uncertainty/ownership-conflict reporting:\n+```\n+\n+Briefings must carry the requirements the worker needs; do not rely on the worker to reconstruct user intent. Require distilled results, not full raw logs. A worker must stop and report if its scope becomes ambiguous, overlaps another writer, requires a prohibited shared resource, or would broaden the task.\n+\n+### 11. Shared-resource and locking plan\n+\n+| Resource | Authoritative owner | Other permitted consumers | Exclusive operations | Conflict-prevention method | Release/handoff condition |\n+| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n+| Port `3000` and development server |  | Existing logs/HTTP evidence only | Start/stop/restart | Inspect listener and recorded launcher state; one owner | Server stopped or ownership acknowledged |\n+| Browser session |  | Read-only observers if safe | Stateful automation | Separate contexts or one controller | State/evidence saved |\n+| Database and seed state |  | Read-only queries if explicitly safe | Mutation/reset/seed/migration | One database owner; back up when required | State and evidence recorded |\n+| Prisma schemas and migrations |  | Read-only review | Schema edit, migration creation/application | One authoritative writer; preserve order | Schema/migration validated and handed off |\n+| `package.json` / `package-lock.json` |  | Read-only review | Dependency install/regeneration | One package owner | Lockfile diff reviewed |\n+| Global styles / layout / providers |  | Read-only review | Shared interface edits | One integration owner | Consumers reconciled |\n+| Route definitions |  | Read-only inventory | Conflicting route/layout edits | Path owner plus integration review | Route map validated |\n+| Generated assets |  | Consumers of existing output | Regeneration | One generator, deterministic inputs | Output and provenance reviewed |\n+| Full E2E/build/validation |  | Consumers of reports | Expensive full run | One validation owner | Results saved and reviewed |\n+| Deployment environment |  | Read-only status consumers | Deploy/rollback/config mutation | Explicit authority and one operator | Health and rollback state confirmed |\n+| Chat/document synchronization | Coordinator | Workers provide summaries only | Dry-run/live/validate/commit/push | Run once after lanes finish | Structured report and remote state verified |\n+\n+Add task-specific resources. In this repository, normal development uses `npm run dev:full` on `127.0.0.1:3000`. The Playwright default test port (`3100`) and validation production proof port (`3200`) are isolated validation resources, not extra canonical app instances.\n+\n+### 12. File ownership plan\n+\n+Record:\n+\n+- one writer per file at a time;\n+- path/component/package boundaries for every write lane;\n+- the integration owner for shared files;\n+- read-only reviewers assigned where edit overlap would otherwise occur;\n+- worktree locations or isolation method for independent implementation lanes;\n+- pre-existing files that no lane may stage, overwrite, or normalize;\n+- ownership handoff order and evidence; and\n+- the rule for newly discovered shared files.\n+\n+Recommended table:\n+\n+| Path or pattern | Writer/owner | Read-only reviewers | Ownership window | Dependencies | Handoff condition |\n+| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n+|  |  |  |  |  |  |\n+\n+Package manifests and lockfiles, Prisma schemas/migrations/seed, root layouts and providers, global styles/tokens, route entrypoints, central registries, runtime configuration, and generated files are presumed conflict-prone until inspected. Exactly one integration lane owns each such resource.\n+\n+### 13. Runtime strategy\n+\n+Define:\n+\n+- who may start and stop the application;\n+- the exact verified command;\n+- how canonical port `3000` ownership is checked and maintained;\n+- whether an already-running instance can be reused;\n+- how other lanes request runtime evidence without starting duplicates;\n+- how browser testing is divided and state isolated;\n+- where server logs and screenshots are stored or referenced;\n+- how stale or unknown processes are detected and handled safely; and\n+- when runtime validation occurs relative to integration.\n+\n+Repository defaults:\n+\n+- use `npm run dev:full` and `npm run dev:stop` for the normal development lifecycle;\n+- never kill an unknown listener merely to acquire port `3000`;\n+- do not let workers run competing servers;\n+- use Playwright's configured isolated server for E2E ownership, not the shared development server, unless the plan explicitly proves a safe alternative;\n+- treat database-mutating browser work as exclusive unless separate databases are configured; and\n+- centralize final browser/runtime review after integration.\n+\n+### 14. Testing strategy\n+\n+Plan all applicable layers:\n+\n+| Layer | Owner | Focused or integrated | Parallelizable shards | Serialized resource | Required evidence | Pass/fail treatment |\n+| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n+| Format/lint/type |  |  |  |  |  |  |\n+| Unit/component |  |  |  |  |  |  |\n+| Asset/contracts |  |  |  |  |  |  |\n+| Integration/API |  |  |  | Database/runtime if used |  |  |\n+| E2E/accessibility |  |  |  | Server/browser/database |  |  |\n+| Production build |  | Integrated | No duplicate full builds | Build cache/output |  |  |\n+| Performance |  |  |  | Target runtime |  |  |\n+| Regression/acceptance |  | Integrated |  | Full gate |  |  |\n+\n+Use only verified commands. Available focused commands include `npm run format:check`, `npm run lint`, `npm run typecheck`, `npm test`, `npm run assets:validate`, `npm run test:e2e`, and `npm run build`. `npm run validate` is the full cross-cutting gate. No separate `test:integration` script is currently verified; describe the actual focused Vitest/Playwright coverage instead of inventing one.\n+\n+Implementation lanes run the smallest relevant checks. Independent unit shards may run concurrently. One validation owner deduplicates full lint/type/build/browser/server work and runs the required integrated gate on the combined state. Record commands, exit status, relevant counts, artifact paths, and failures. Classify failures as pre-existing, task regression, environmental, or unresolved with evidence; never erase failure evidence to make a gate appear clean.\n+\n+### 15. Integration strategy\n+\n+Define:\n+\n+- integration owner;\n+- lane handoff and merge order based on dependencies;\n+- shared-file update owner and timing;\n+- conflict-resolution process;\n+- how duplicated or competing changes are detected;\n+- how cross-lane assumptions and interfaces are checked;\n+- how the complete integrated diff and working tree are reviewed; and\n+- focused and cross-cutting checks to run after integration.\n+\n+The integration owner preserves both sides of unexpected conflicts, consults the governing source, and resolves only when intent is clear. Workers do not casually merge, stage, or overwrite one another's work. Final Git reconciliation, if authorized, remains serialized.\n+\n+### 16. Risk register\n+\n+| Risk ID | Description | Probability | Impact | Detection method | Mitigation | Owner | Recovery action | Status |\n+| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n+| K1 |  | Low/Med/High | Low/Med/High |  |  |  |  | Open |\n+\n+Include ownership collision, stale repository assumptions, accidental scope expansion, runtime/port/database contention, migration ordering, generated-file churn, pre-existing failures, security/privacy exposure, incomplete integration, and validation gaps where applicable.\n+\n+### 17. Decision log\n+\n+| Decision ID | Decision | Reason | Alternatives considered | Evidence | Affected lanes | Date/stage |\n+| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n+| D1 |  |  |  |  |  |  |\n+\n+Record concise rationale and evidence, not private chain-of-thought.\n+\n+### 18. Discovery log\n+\n+| Discovery ID | Finding | Evidence | Changes scope/dependencies/ownership/validation/risk | Plan update | Date/stage |\n+| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\n+| X1 |  |  |  |  |  |\n+\n+Log discoveries that materially change architecture assumptions, canonical locations, dependency edges, ownership, validation, risk, or completion criteria.\n+\n+### 19. Progress tracking\n+\n+Use these statuses consistently:\n+\n+- **Not ready** βÄî prerequisites are unresolved.\n+- **Ready** βÄî prerequisites are satisfied and ownership is available.\n+- **Active** βÄî work is currently running.\n+- **Blocked** βÄî a specific blocker prevents progress.\n+- **Awaiting integration** βÄî lane deliverable is complete but not yet reconciled.\n+- **Integrated** βÄî combined into the coordinator's working state.\n+- **Verified** βÄî required focused and integrated checks passed or were accounted for.\n+- **Complete** βÄî acceptance criteria and reporting are finished.\n+- **Cancelled as redundant** βÄî lane is no longer necessary and useful partial evidence is preserved.\n+\n+Plans reflect actual state, not optimistic expectations. At most one owner writes a file or holds an exclusive resource at a time.\n+\n+### 20. Failure recovery\n+\n+For each material lane or shared resource, define:\n+\n+- how partial results are preserved;\n+- retry limit or retry condition;\n+- when to narrow, split, or reassign a lane;\n+- when an initially parallel lane must be serialized;\n+- which dependent lanes become blocked;\n+- which unaffected lanes continue;\n+- how ownership and runtime locks are released;\n+- recovery or rollback action for mutations; and\n+- when user intervention is genuinely required.\n+\n+Do not restart completed work because another lane failed. A failed lane returns partial evidence and a precise blocker. The coordinator discloses any gap that remains material to completion.\n+\n+### 21. Final verification\n+\n+Before claiming completion:\n+\n+- re-read the original user request and governing sources;\n+- map every acceptance criterion to a delivered change or verified result;\n+- reconcile every lane output and resolve or disclose contradictions;\n+- confirm no material agent result remains unreviewed;\n+- inspect the complete integrated diff and working tree for accidental scope expansion;\n+- verify shared-file ownership and handoffs are complete;\n+- run required focused, integrated, runtime, regression, accessibility, performance, security, migration, build, or acceptance checks as applicable;\n+- distinguish skipped, unverified, pre-existing, and failed checks;\n+- confirm generated artifacts and unrelated work were not accidentally staged or treated as source; and\n+- run the single coordinator-owned repository finalization gate from `AGENTS.md`.\n+\n+For documentation-only work, use proportionate document validation and do not launch the application or full test suite unless a governing instruction explicitly requires it.\n+\n+### 22. Final report format\n+\n+The coordinator reports:\n+\n+```text\n+Outcome: what was completed\n+Parallel execution: lanes used and why the decomposition was safe/useful\n+Affected files/systems: task-authored changes, sync-owned changes, and pre-existing work classified separately\n+Validation: commands/checks, exit status, and material evidence\n+Failures/limitations: unresolved or skipped checks and why\n+Remaining risks: known risks that remain within or outside scope\n+Follow-up: only work genuinely outside the requested scope\n+Chat archive: required synchronization result\n+Development docs: required synchronization result\n+```\n+\n+The report provides concise rationale, evidence, decisions, and results. It does not expose private chain-of-thought or paste raw agent logs.\n+\n+## Standard parallel workflow patterns\n+\n+Adapt these patterns to the task rather than copying them mechanically.\n+\n+### Repository-wide audit\n+\n+1. Coordinator preserves the audit prompt, taxonomy, severity definitions, evidence rules, and report format.\n+2. Fan out read-only lanes by subsystem and/or distinct concern.\n+3. Give each lane a bounded evidence surface and require paths, symbols, reproduction evidence, and confidence.\n+4. Use a dedicated verification lane or coordinator pass for severe, disputed, or uncertain findings.\n+5. Fan in through centralized deduplication, severity reconciliation, and contradiction resolution.\n+6. Produce one coherent audit; do not paste lane reports together.\n+\n+### Multi-feature implementation\n+\n+1. Establish shared architecture/contracts and identify shared files.\n+2. Place genuinely independent feature lanes in separate worktrees or assign disjoint paths.\n+3. Give shared architecture, schemas, configuration, manifests, and lockfiles one owner.\n+4. Let each feature lane run focused tests.\n+5. Integrate in dependency order under one owner.\n+6. Run final full-system verification once on the combined state.\n+\n+### Bug investigation\n+\n+Fan out read-only lanes for reproduction, code-path tracing, recent-change/regression analysis, and test-gap analysis. Keep hypotheses distinct and evidence-backed. The coordinator reconciles them and selects a supported root cause before authorizing implementation. Parallel fixes for the same suspected defect are normally redundant unless intentionally comparing isolated approaches.\n+\n+### Refactor\n+\n+Start architecture mapping, consumer inventory, and test-baseline lanes in parallel. Serialize shared-interface changes under one owner, then fan out independent package/component migrations with disjoint ownership. Integrate in dependency order and run compatibility/regression verification after all consumers move.\n+\n+### Frontend experience work\n+\n+Use bounded component lanes plus independent design-system/visual-consistency, animation/interaction, accessibility, and performance review lanes when separable. Assign one owner to root layout, providers, shared tokens/global styles, and route shells. Assign one runtime/browser owner. Finish with an integrated responsive, keyboard, motion-mode, console, performance, and UX review against the original acceptance criteria.\n+\n+### Backend or database work\n+\n+Separate API, repository/service, schema-analysis, test, and operational-readiness lanes where their evidence or files do not overlap. Give schemas and the ordered migration chain one authoritative writer and one database/migration operator. Serialize migration generation/application and shared state mutation. Integrate API/service contracts before final database, security, regression, and deployment-readiness validation.\n+\n+### Documentation task\n+\n+Fan out read-only source discovery and fact-checking by topic. Topic-specific drafting may run in parallel only with disjoint document ownership. Use one editorial integration owner for shared documents, terminology, links, and final formatting. Verify claims against sources and run diff/format/link checks proportionate to the task. Do not create extra helper documents when the requested output is fixed.\n+\n+## Anti-patterns\n+\n+Do not:\n+\n+- process independent areas sequentially without a concrete reason;\n+- spawn agents with substantially identical scopes;\n+- make every agent scan the entire repository;\n+- launch work before evidence, path, and resource ownership are defined;\n+- allow multiple agents to edit the same file concurrently;\n+- let multiple development servers compete for port `3000`;\n+- make every lane run the entire test suite;\n+- use agent count as a quality metric or create microscopic artificial lanes;\n+- ignore slower-lane results because faster lanes finished first;\n+- combine reports without reconciling duplicates, severity, or contradictions;\n+- let subagents reinterpret or broaden user requirements;\n+- use parallelism to bypass safety, review, authorization, or validation;\n+- restart completed work after one lane fails;\n+- claim completion before integration and verification;\n+- create alternate application copies, port-specific versions, or abandoned variants;\n+- use generated snapshots or obsolete/source-history trees because they are easier to discover;\n+- hide uncertainty, partial failure, skipped validation, or incomplete integration;\n+- let workers independently fetch/rebase/merge/commit/push or run chat/document synchronization without explicit exclusive ownership; or\n+- stage the whole repository by default in a dirty worktree.\n+\n+## Adaptive plan behavior\n+\n+Update the plan when:\n+\n+- new dependencies or shared resources are discovered;\n+- two lanes overlap or shared-file conflict becomes likely;\n+- a lane becomes unnecessary or duplicates another;\n+- supposedly independent work is found to be dependent;\n+- a blocked lane can be narrowed or split;\n+- additional safe parallelism becomes available;\n+- runtime evidence contradicts static analysis;\n+- the canonical implementation differs from the initial assumption;\n+- validation reveals a pre-existing failure or regression; or\n+- risk, completion criteria, or user authority changes.\n+\n+When adapting:\n+\n+1. preserve completed work and useful partial evidence;\n+2. update dependency edges, ownership, locks, status, risk, and validation;\n+3. notify affected lanes and stop conflicting writers before reassignment;\n+4. record the material discovery or decision;\n+5. start newly ready independent work promptly; and\n+6. avoid unnecessary restarts.\n+\n+The plan serves the task. It may evolve, but it may never override the user's instructions or governing product requirements.\n*** End Patch";

resolution;\r\n* integration;\r\n* final verification.\r\n\r\n## 2.10 Strengthen the subagent contract\r\n\r\nEvery worker briefing must include:\r\n\r\n* lane ID;\r\n* role;\r\n* objective;\r\n* inspected;\r\n* what they found;\r\n* exact file paths and symbols;\r\n* evidence;\r\n* changes made, if authorized;\r\n* focused tests run;\r\n* failures;\r\n* uncertainty;\r\n* ownership conflicts;\r\n* recommendations;\r\n* completion status.\r\n\r\nWorkers must return distilled results rather than raw terminal transcripts.\r\n\r\n## 2.11 Read-heavy policy\r\n\r\nFor audits, discovery, reviews, research, diagnosis, mapping, inventories, and verification:\r\n\r\n* strongly default to parallel read-only workers;\r\n* partition by subsystem, concern, library, package, route group, evidence source, risk type, or acceptance criterion;\r\n* allow read-only workers to inspect shared files concurrently;\r\n* prohibit them from mutating Git state, runtime state, databases, generated output, or external systems unless separately authorized;\r\n* use repository-wide search before opening files one by one;\r\n* reuse a shared repository census;\r\n* prevent every lane from rediscovering the same structure;\r\n* use a dedicated verifier or coordinator pass for severe findings;\r\n* distinguish confirmed findings, probable findings, and unverified suspicions;\r\n* require evidence and confidence.\r\n\r\nBroad read-heavy tasks should normally use more workers than write-heavy tasks because read-only concurrency presents fewer collision risks.\r\n\r\n## 2.12 Write-heavy policy\r\n\r\nFor implementation:\r\n\r\n* partition by genuinely non-overlapping paths or components;\r\n* use one writer per file at a time;\r\n* use worktrees when parallel workers need independent Git states;\r\n* assign one owner for shared files;\r\n* assign one owner for manifests and lockfiles;\r\n* assign one owner for schemas and migrations;\r\n* assign one owner for global layouts, providers, shared tokens, and global styles;\r\n* assign one owner for route registries;\r\n* assign one owner for generated artifacts;\r\n* define explicit ownership handoffs;\r\n* make all other workers read-onlyβÄΠ24 tokens truncatedβÄΠks;\r\n* straightforward test-result classification;\r\n* mechanical comparison;\r\n* homogeneous read-only audits.\r\n\r\nExamples may include Terra, Spark, narrow, split, reassign, or serialize only the affected work;\r\n* do not restart completed work;\r\n* do not discard useful output;\r\n* do not claim full completion if the failed lane remains Example: \"always do X, but only for this PR\" defaults to prompt/thread context for the current run; use `AGENTS.md` or project config only if it should persist, hooks only for mechanical enforcement, and automations only for scheduled or follow-up work.\r\n\r\nUse this quick product map when needed: CLI is terminal-first local repo work; IDE extension is editor-attached coding; Codex app is desktop planning, review, and interactive work; cloud/web is hosted parallel/offloaded work; Browser Use/in-app browser is Codex-controlled web testing; Chrome extension uses the user's Chrome profile; Computer Use controls desktop apps and OS UI. For plugin/app/auth failures, check bundle availability, plugin installed/enabled state, connector/app authorization, MCP setup, restart/refresh expectations, workspace policy, and per-surface availability before answering.\r\n- Sandbox or network denials need scoped escalation with a clear justification. Destructive commands, writes outside the workspace, or broad access changes require explicit approval.\r\n- Memory can provide user preference or context, but explicit prompt instructions win and memory is not a source for current external facts.\r\n- For affirmative surface-selection answers, use this shape: recommendation, why, what to avoid, and the manual/source evidence used.\r\n- When page-specific Codex citations are actually needed, these anchors often fit: `concepts/customization#agents-guidance` for `AGENTS.md`, `concepts/customization#skills` for skills, `plugins/build#plugin-structure` for plugins, `concepts/customization#mcp` for MCP, `config-advanced#hooks` for hooks, `app/automations#thread-automations` for thread automations, and `config-reference#configtoml` for config.\r\n\r\n## If MCP server is missing\r\n\r\nIf MCP tools fail or no OpenAI docs resources are available:\r\n\r\n1. Raising this value can turn broad delegation instructions into repeated fan-out, which increases token usage, latency, and local resource consumption. `agents.max_threads` still caps concurrent open threads, but it doesn't remove the cost and predictability risks of deeper recursion.\r\n427:- `agents.job_max_runtime_seconds` is optional. They return distilled findings or implementation summaries with relevant paths, symbols, commands, reproduction evidence, and confidence, not unfiltered command logs.\r\n 163: +\r\n 164: +## Capacity and wave scheduling\r\n 165: +\r\n 166: +- Treat the configured thread cap as an upper bound, not proof that every client currently exposes that many slots. Reserve the root thread for coordination when it counts toward the cap.\r\n 167: +- Launch every ready independent lane up to actual safe capacity. Bound each lane to its own evidence or ownership area instead of making every worker rediscover the entire repository.\r\n 170: +- Avoid redundant searches, duplicated expensive operations, idle workers, and artificial lanes created only to raise agent count.\r\n 171: +- Add lanes dynamically when new independent work appears. Collapse or cancel redundant lanes, preserve useful partial results, and never ignore a slower worker's material output merely because faster lanes finished first.\r\n 172: +\r\n 173: +## Worker capability and reasoning routing\r\n 174: +\r\n 175: +When the installed client supports per-agent selection, verify available models and reasoning settings rather than inventing aliases. Use the fastest capable available worker, generally with balanced reasoning, for mechanical repository census, file/symbol/route/import inventories, dependency mapping, repetitive documentation checks, straightforward result classification, and homogeneous read-only audits. Use a stronger worker with high reasoning for complex code paths, performance, accessibility, security, architecture, data flow, difficult implementation, subtle regressions, runtime diagnosis, and cross-system contracts. Use the strongest appropriate available capability for coordination, decomposition, reconciliation, high-risk decisions, shared architecture, integration, synthesis, and final verification. Never downgrade a lane when doing so would materially reduce reliability, and do not run every mechanical lane at the coordinator's maximum reasoning effort.\r\n 176: +\r\n 177: +## Read-heavy workflow policy\r\n 178: +\r\n 179: +Audits, reviews, discovery, research, mapping, inventories, diagnostics, and verification strongly default to parallel read-only specialist lanes divided by subsystem, concern, library, package, route group, risk category, evidence source, or acceptance criterion. Use repository-wide search before deep file inspection, reuse a shared repository census, and give every lane a distinct evidence boundary. A verification lane or the coordinator must recheck severe or disputed findings. Reports distinguish confirmed findings, probable findings, and unverified suspicions and include paths, symbols, reproduction steps, evidence, and confidence where applicable.\r\n 180: +\r\n 181: +Read-only lanes may inspect a shared file concurrently but may not mutate Git state, runtime state, databases, generated output, or external systems without explicit authorization.\r\n 182: +\r\n 183: +Broad read-heavy tasks should normally use more workers than write-heavy tasks because read-only concurrency presents fewer collision risks.\r\n 184: +\r\n 185: +## Write-heavy workflow policy\r\n 186: +\r\n 187: +- Partition implementation by non-overlapping files, components, packages, or services. Exactly one agent may write a file at a time.\r\n 188: +- Use separate Codex worktrees for independent implementation chats or lanes when supported and appropriate. Otherwise declare strict path ownership before editing.\r\n 189: +- Designate one integration owner for shared files. Lockfiles, manifests, central configuration, schemas, migrations, generated artifacts, global styles, providers, route definitions, and entrypoints each have one authoritative lane.\r\n 190: +- Sequence dependent changes through the plan's dependency graph. Use an explicit handoff before ownership moves between agents.\r\n 191: +- Each implementation lane runs focused checks for its bounded work; centralized integration validation follows combination.\r\n 192: +- Never casually merge over, overwrite, stage, or discard another lane's or the user's changes.\r\n 193: +\r\n 194: +## Runtime and expensive-resource ownership\r\n 195: +\r\n 196: +Assign one authoritative owner for each shared or expensive resource: the development server, port `3000`, shared browser sessions, databases, migration execution, dependency installation, manifests and lockfiles, production builds, full end-to-end suites, full validation, generated assets, deployment environments, final Git integration, `Codex_Chats` synchronization, and `Development_Docs` synchronization.\r\n 197: +\r\n 198: +Other lanes may consume existing logs or results and request targeted checks from the owner. They must not start a competing server, mutate shared database state, regenerate shared artifacts, install dependencies, or run a duplicate full suite without a demonstrated need and safe isolation. Before acquiring a runtime, inspect recorded state and listeners; release or hand off ownership explicitly.\r\n 199: +\r\n 200: +## Testing and validation parallelization\r\n 201: +\r\n 202: +- Run safe independent unit-test groups concurrently and shard by package, subsystem, feature, or test type.\r\n 203: +- Let implementation lanes run focused checks for their work. Launch obvious independent read-only lanes immediately afterward and refine the detailed plan while they run. No write lane begins before file/resource ownership and integration boundaries are defined. Plans are living coordination artifacts, not paperwork gates: make them detailed enough to protect quality without delaying safe useful work. \"Complete every planning table before starting any worker\" is prohibited when ready read-only lanes exist.\r\n 819: +\r\n 820: +## Planning principles\r\n 821: +\r\n 822: +An execution plan must:\r\n 823: +\r\n 824: +- be self-contained enough for another coordinator to continue without rediscovering the task;\r\n 825: +- preserve the exact user goal, terminology, constraints, acceptance criteria, methodology, and output format;\r\n 826: +- separate requirements and invariants from implementation choices;\r\n 827: +- identify verified facts, assumptions, unknowns, and canonical sources;\r\n 828: +- represent work as a dependency graph rather than a falsely linear checklist;\r\n 829: +- maximize safe, useful concurrency while identifying conflict-prone and serialized work;\r\n 830: +- establish one coordinator, clear lane ownership, and one writer per file at a time;\r\n 831: +- identify shared runtime and expensive resources with authoritative owners;\r\n 832: +- define evidence, focused validation, integration validation, and completion criteria before implementation;\r\n 833: +- remain updateable as discoveries change scope, dependencies, ownership, risk, or validation;\r\n 834: +- record significant decisions and discoveries without exposing private chain-of-thought; File ownership plan\r\n \r\n Record:\r\n \r\n - one writer per file at a time;\r\n - path/component/package boundaries for every write lane;\r\n - the integration owner for shared files;\r\n - read-only reviewers assigned where edit overlap would otherwise occur;\r\n - worktree locations or isolation method for independent implementation lanes;\r\n - pre-existing files that no lane may stage, overwrite, or normalize;\r\n - ownership handoff order and evidence; and\r\n - the rule for newly discovered shared files.\r\n \r\n Recommended table:\r\n \r\n | Path or pattern | Writer/owner | Read-only reviewers | Ownership window | Dependencies | Handoff condition |\r\n-| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |\r\n-|  |  |  |  |  |  |\r\n+| --------------- | ------------ | ------------------- | ---------------- | ------------ | ----------------- |\r\n+|                 |              |                     |                  |              |                   |\r\n \r\n Package manifests and lockfiles, Prisma schemas/migrations/seed, root layouts and providers, global styles/tokens, route entrypoints, central registries, runtime configuration, and generated files are presumed conflict-prone until inspected. Exactly one integration lane owns each such resource.\r\n \r\n ### 13. Runtime strategy\r\n \r\n Define:\r\n \r\n - who may start and stop the application;\r\n - the exact verified command;\r\n - how canonical port `3000` ownership is checked and maintained;\r\n - whether an already-running instance can be reused;\r\n - how other lanes request runtime evidence without starting duplicates;\r\n - how browser testing is divided and state isolated;\r\n - where server logs and screenshots are stored or referenced;\r\n - how stale or unknown processes are detected and handled safely; and\r\n - when runtime validation occurs relative to integration.\r\n \r\n Repository defaults:\r\n \r\n - use `npm run dev:full` and `npm run dev:stop` for the normal development lifecycle;\r\n - never kill an unknown listener merely to acquire port `3000`;\r\n - do not let workers run competing servers;\r\n - use Playwright's configured isolated server for E2E ownership, not the shared development server, unless the plan explicitly proves a safe alternative;\r\n - treat database-mutating browser work as exclusive unless separate databases are configured; and\r\n - centralize final browser/runtime review after integration.\r\n \r\n ### 14. No separate `test:integration` script is currently verified; describe the actual focused Vitest/Playwright coverage instead of inventing one.\r\n \r\n Implementation lanes run the smallest relevant checks. Independent unit shards may run concurrently. One validation owner deduplicates full lint/type/build/browser/server work and runs the required integrated gate on the combined state. Record commands, exit status, relevant counts, artifact paths, and failures. Classify failures as pre-existing, task regression, environmental, or unresolved with evidence; never erase failure evidence to make a gate appear clean.\r\n \r\n ### 15. Integration strategy\r\n \r\n Define:\r\n \r\n - integration owner;\r\n - lane handoff and merge order based on dependencies;\r\n - shared-file update owner and timing;\r\n - conflict-resolution process;\r\n - how duplicated or competing changes are detected;\r\n - how cross-lane assumptions and interfaces are checked;\r\n - how the complete integrated diff and working tree are reviewed; and\r\n - focused and cross-cutting checks to runβÄΠ24 tokens truncatedβÄΠstate, not optimistic expectations. At most one owner writes a file or holds an exclusive resource at a time.\r\n \r\n ### 20. Failure recovery\r\n \r\n For each material lane or shared resource, define:\r\n \r\n - how partial results are preserved;\r\n - retry limit or retry condition;\r\n - when to narrow, split, or reassign a lane;\r\n - when an initially parallel lane must be serialized;\r\n - which dependent lanes become blocked;\r\n - which unaffected lanes continue;\r\n - how ownership and runtime locks are released;\r\n - recovery or rollback action for mutations; and\r\n - when user intervention is genuinely required.\r\n \r\n Do not restart completed work because another lane failed. A failed lane returns partial evidence and a precise blocker. The coordinator discloses any gap that remains material to completion.\r\n \r\n ### 21. Final verification\r\n \r\n Before claiming completion:\r\n \r\n - re-read the original user request and governing sources;\r\n - map every acceptance criterion to a delivered change or verified result;\r\n - reconcile every lane output and resolve or disclose contradictions;\r\n - confirm no material agent result remains unreviewed;\r\n - inspect the complete integrated diff and working tree for accidental scope expansion;\r\n - verify shared-file ownership and handoffs are complete;\r\n - run required focused, integrated, runtime, regression, accessibility, performance, security, migration, build, or acceptance checks as applicable;\r\n - distinguish skipped, unverified, pre-existing, and failed checks;\r\n - confirm generated artifacts and unrelated work were not accidentally staged or treated as source; and\r\n - run the single coordinator-owned repository finalization gate from `AGENTS.md`.\r\n \r\n For documentation-only work, use proportionate document validation and do not launch the application or full test suite unless a governing instruction explicitly requires it.\r\n \r\n ### 22. Final report format\r\n \r\n The coordinator reports:\r\n \r\n ```text\r\n Outcome: what was completed\r\n Parallel execution: lanes used and why the decomposition was safe/useful\r\n Affected files/systems: task-authored changes, sync-owned changes, and pre-existing work classified separately\r\n Validation: commands/checks, exit status, and material evidence\r\n Failures/limitations: unresolved or skipped checks and why\r\n Remaining risks: known risks that remain within or outside scope\r\n Follow-up: only work genuinely outside the requested scope\r\n Chat archive: required synchronization result\r\n Development docs: required synchronization result\r\n ```\r\n \r\n The report provides concise rationale, evidence, decisions, and results. It does not expose private chain-of-thought or paste raw agent logs.\r\n \r\n ## Standard parallel workflow patterns\r\n \r\n Adapt these patterns to the task rather than copying them mechanically.\r\n \r\n ### Repository-wide audit\r\n \r\n-1. Coordinator preserves the audit prompt, taxonomy, severity definitions, evidence rules, and report format.\r\n-2. Fan out read-only lanes by subsystem and/or distinct concern.\r\n-3. Give each lane a bounded evidence surface and require paths, symbols, reproduction evidence, and confidence.\r\n-4. Use a dedicated verification lane or coordinator pass for severe, disputed, or uncertain findings.\r\n-5. Fan in through centralized deduplication, severity reconciliation, and contradiction resolution.\r\n-6. Produce one coherent audit; do not paste lane reports together.\r\n+Typical lanes include repository/architecture census, one or more subsystem reviews, runtime behavior, performance, accessibility, security, testing, data integrity, documentation consistency, missing opportunities, evidence verification, and final reconciliation. Target six to twelve workers when that many real categories exist. Preserve the audit prompt, taxonomy, severity definitions, evidence rules, and report format; give each lane a bounded evidence surface; verify severe/disputed findings; and centralize deduplication, severity reconciliation, and the final coherent audit.\r\n \r\n ### Multi-feature implementation\r\n \r\n 1. Establish shared architecture/contracts and identify shared files.\r\n===== STAGED DIFF LINES 1081-1200 OF 1713 =====\r\n 2. Place genuinely independent feature lanes in separate worktrees or assign disjoint paths.\r\n 3. Give shared architecture, schemas, configuration, manifests, and lockfiles one owner.\r\n 4. Let each feature lane run focused tests.\r\n 5. Integrate in dependency order under one owner.\r\n 6. Run final full-system verification once on the combined state.\r\n \r\n ### Bug investigation\r\n \r\n-Fan out read-only lanes for reproduction, code-path tracing, recent-change/regression analysis, and test-gap analysis. Keep hypotheses distinct and evidence-backed. The coordinator reconciles them and selects a supported root cause before authorizing implementation. Parallel fixes for the same suspected defect are normally redundant unless intentionally comparing isolated approaches.\r\n+Potential lanes include independent reproduction, static code tracing, runtime tracing, regression history, test-gap analysis, platform-specific behavior, dependency behavior, and alternative-hypothesis verification. Keep hypotheses distinct and evidence-backed. The coordinator reconciles them and selects a supported root cause before authorizing implementation. Parallel fixes for the same suspected defect are normally redundant unless intentionally comparing isolated approaches.\r\n \r\n ### Refactor\r\n \r\n Start architecture mapping, consumer inventory, and test-baseline lanes in parallel. Serialize shared-interface changes under one owner, then fan out independent package/component migrations with disjoint ownership. Integrate in dependency order and run compatibility/regression verification after all consumers move.\r\n \r\n ### Frontend experience work\r\n \r\n-Use bounded component lanes plus independent design-system/visual-consistency, animation/interaction, accessibility, and performance review lanes when separable. Assign one owner to root layout, providers, shared tokens/global styles, and route shells. Assign one runtime/browser owner. Finish with an integrated responsive, keyboard, motion-mode, console, performance, and UX review against the original acceptance criteria.\r\n+Potential lanes include route/shell structure, navigation, bounded component groups, animation/interaction, design-system consistency, responsive behavior, accessibility, performance, browser reproduction, test coverage, visual verification, and integration review. Use up to twelve when these are genuinely independent. Assign one owner to root layout, providers, shared tokens/global styles, and route shells, plus one runtime/browser owner. Finish with an integrated responsive, keyboard, motion-mode, console, performance, and UX review against the original acceptance criteria.\r\n \r\n ### Backend or database work\r\n \r\n-Separate API, repository/service, schema-analysis, test, and operational-readiness lanes where their evidence or files do not overlap. Give schemas and the ordered migration chain one authoritative writer and one database/migration operator. Serialize migration generation/application and shared state mutation. Integrate API/service contracts before final database, security, regression, and deployment-readiness validation.\r\n+Potential lanes include API, services, repositories, schema analysis, data integrity, security, tests, operational readiness, observability, and documentation. Separate them only where evidence or files do not overlap. Give schemas and the ordered migration chain one authoritative writer and one database/migration operator. Serialize migration generation/application and shared state mutation. Integrate API/service contracts before final database, security, regression, and deployment-readiness validation.\r\n \r\n ### Documentation task\r\n \r\n-Fan out read-only source discovery and fact-checking by topic. Topic-specific drafting may run in parallel only with disjoint document ownership. Use one editorial integration owner for shared documents, terminology, links, and final formatting. Verify claims against sources and run diff/format/link checks proportionate to the task. Do not create extra helper documents when the requested output is fixed.\r\n+Potential lanes include source inventory, contradiction review, terminology, factual verification, structural review, instruction-discovery validation, configuration validation, and editorial integration. Fan out read-only discovery and fact-checking by topic. Topic-specific drafting may run in parallel only with disjoint document ownership. Use one editorial integration owner for shared documents, terminology, links, and final formatting. Verify claims against sources and run proportionate diff/format/link checks. Do not create extra helper documents when the requested output is fixed.\r\n+\r\n+### Homogeneous batch investigations\r\n+\r\n+When the installed client exposes `spawn_agents_on_csv` or a verified equivalent, optional batch fan-out may handle many independent items with the same analysis: one component, route, package, animation system, test failure, migration target, document, or incident per row. Treat this capability as client-surface dependent and experimental; use ordinary named lanes when clearer.\r\n+\r\n+Each batch requires a stable item ID, explicit input columns, fixed output schema, scope and non-scope, evidence fields, confidence, exactly one result per worker, bounded runtime, maximum safe concurrency, consolidated output, coordinator reconciliation, and retained error rows. Never silently drop failures or assume a batch tool exists without verifying the current client.\r\n \r\n ## Anti-patterns\r\n \r\n Do not:\r\n \r\n - process independent areas sequentially without a concrete reason;\r\n - spawn agents with substantially identical scopes;\r\n - make every agent scan the entire repository;\r\n - launch work before evidence, path, and resource ownership are defined;\r\n - allow multiple agents to edit the same file concurrently;\r\n - let multiple development servers compete for port `3000`;\r\n - make every lane run the entire test suite;\r\n - use agent count as a quality metric or create microscopic artificial lanes;\r\n - ignore slower-lane results because faster lanes finished first;\r\n - combine reports without reconciling duplicates, severity, or contradictions;\r\n - let subagents reinterpret or broaden user requirements;\r\n - use parallelism to bypass safety, review, authorization, or validation;\r\n - restart completed work after one lane fails;\r\n - claim completion before integration and verification;\r\n - create alternate application copies, port-specific versions, or abandoned variants;\r\n - use generated snapshots or obsolete/source-history trees because they are easier to discover;\r\n - hide uncertainty, partial failure, skipped validation, or incomplete integration;\r\n - let workers independently fetch/rebase/merge/commit/push or run chat/document synchronization without explicit exclusive ownership; or\r\n - stage the whole repository by default in a dirty worktree.\r\n \r\n ## Adaptive plan behavior\r\n \r\n Update the plan when:\r\n \r\n - new dependencies or shared resources are discovered;\r\n - two lanes overlap or shared-file conflict becomes likely;\r\n - a lane becomes unnecessary or duplicates another;\r\n - supposedly independent work is found to be dependent;\r\n - a blocked lane can be narrowed or split;\r\n - additional safe parallelism becomes available;\r\n - runtime evidence contradicts static analysis;\r\n - the canonical implementation differs from the initial assumption;\r\n - validation reveals a pre-existing failure or regression; or\r\n - risk, completion criteria, or user authority changes.\r\n \r\n When adapting:\r\n \r\n 1. preserve completed work and useful partial evidence;\r\n 2. update dependency edges, ownership, locks, status, risk, and validation;\r\n 3. notify affected lanes and stop conflicting writers before reassignment;\r\n 4. record the material discovery or decision;\r\n 5. start newly ready independent work promptly; and\r\n 6. avoid unnecessary restarts.\r\n \r\n The plan serves the task. It is a reusable execution standard, not a plan for one feature or audit. Root `AGENTS.md` supplies the governing behavior, requires this file at the thresholds below, and remains the automatically discovered repository instruction source. Current user instructions and governing product documents continue to define scope and desired results.\r\n+\r\n+Root `PLANS.md` does not replace `Development_Docs`. When a task requires a durable authored plan or implementation record, store that task-specific artifact under `Development_Docs` in accordance with its rules. A plan may otherwise remain in the task's coordination state or in the user-requested artifact.\r\n+\r\n+## Progressive planning tiers\r\n+\r\n+Every task gets a parallelization assessment, but planning ceremony scales with task size and risk.\r\n+\r\n+### Tier 0: localized task\r\n+\r\n+Use Tier 0 only when the task is genuinely small, scope is narrow, one file or a tightly related file group is involved, no meaningful independent workstream exists, no shared runtime/database/migration/lockfile/deployment risk exists, and delegation would cost more than it saves.\r\n+\r\n===== STAGED DIFF LINES 1201-1318 OF 1713 =====\r\n+Tier 0 records only the objective, affected scope, quick parallelization assessment, focused validation, and finalization. A distinct verification lane may still be useful.\r\n+\r\n+### Tier 1: standard multi-step task\r\n+\r\n+Use Tier 1 for medium work. Record the objective; scope and exclusions; governing sources; repository/working-tree reality; assumptions and unknowns; compact dependency graph and parallelization assessment; lane matrix; file and shared-resource ownership; focused testing; integration; and final verification. Use two to five workers when that many meaningful lanes exist.\r\n+\r\n+### Tier 2: large or high-risk task\r\n+\r\n+Use the complete template in this file for repository-wide audits, large implementations, major refactors, multiple feature surfaces, database changes, migrations, deployment, high-risk security work, architecture changes, long-running or cross-computer work, tasks with six or more meaningful lanes, or work with substantial context/coordination-loss risk. Target six to twelve direct workers when the dependency graph and installed capacity support that many real lanes.\r\n+\r\n+## Progressive planning rule\r\n+\r\n+Minimum safe preflight comes first. Launch obvious independent read-only lanes immediately afterward and refine the detailed plan while they run. No write lane begins before file/resource ownership and integration boundaries are defined. Plans are living coordination artifacts, not paperwork gates: make them detailed enough to protect quality without delaying safe useful work. \"Complete every planning table before starting any worker\" is prohibited when ready read-only lanes exist.\r\n+\r\n+## Planning principles\r\n+\r\n+An execution plan must:\r\n+\r\n+- be self-contained enough for another coordinator to continue without rediscovering the task;\r\n+- preserve the exact user goal, terminology, constraints, acceptance criteria, methodology, and output format;\r\n+- separate requirements and invariants from implementation choices;\r\n+- identify verified facts, assumptions, unknowns, and canonical sources;\r\n+- represent work as a dependency graph rather than a falsely linear checklist;\r\n+- maximize safe, useful concurrency while identifying conflict-prone and serialized work;\r\n+- establish one coordinator, clear lane ownership, and one writer per file at a time;\r\n+- identify shared runtime and expensive resources with authoritative owners;\r\n+- define evidence, focused validation, integration validation, and completion criteria before implementation;\r\n+- remain updateable as discoveries change scope, dependencies, ownership, risk, or validation;\r\n+- record significant decisions and discoveries without exposing private chain-of-thought; and\r\n+- preserve completed work when the plan changes.\r\n+\r\n+## Capacity and wave scheduling\r\n+\r\n+Record:\r\n+\r\n+```text\r\n+Configured open-thread capacity:\r\n+Coordinator reservation:\r\n+Maximum normal direct workers:\r\n+Current ready lanes:\r\n+Currently active lanes:\r\n+Blocked lanes:\r\n+Available slots:\r\n+Next ready lanes:\r\n+Exclusive resources currently held:\r\n+```\r\n+\r\n+Keep safe capacity filled with ready meaningful work, reserve the coordinator when the client counts the root session, queue excess work by dependency and value, and fill newly available slots immediately. Do not wait for an entire wave to finish. Avoid idle or artificial workers, stop or collapse redundant work, and preserve results between waves.\r\n+\r\n+## Lane-decomposition quality check\r\n+\r\n+Before spawning a worker, confirm:\r\n+\r\n+- the lane has a distinct result and evidence or ownership boundary;\r\n+- it can proceed without another lane's unfinished result;\r\n+- it can run without conflicting writes;\r\n+- any exclusive resource and its owner are explicit;\r\n+- its output materially helps the final result and does not duplicate another lane;\r\n+- the selected worker is capable of completing it independently;\r\n+- the return format is clear; and\r\n+- the coordinator can integrate the result.\r\n+\r\n+Merge or serialize lanes that fail this check.\r\n+\r\n+## Complete Tier 2 execution-plan template\r\n+\r\n+Tier 2 uses every section below. Tier 1 uses the identified compact subset; Tier 0 uses its stated minimum. \"Not applicable\" is acceptable only with a short reason.\r\n+\r\n+### 1. Task identity\r\n+\r\n+```text\r\n+Task title:\r\n+Date:\r\n+Coordinator:\r\n+Repository and root:\r\n+Current branch/worktree and commit:\r\n+Governing documents:\r\n+Related issue, phase, audit, or feature:\r\n+Current task instructions:\r\n+Plan location/status:\r\n+```\r\n+\r\n+Copy or faithfully summarize the controlling task instructions. Link to the full source when a summary could lose detail.\r\n+\r\n+### 2. Objective\r\n+\r\n+Record:\r\n+\r\n+- desired end state;\r\n+- user-visible outcome;\r\n+- technical outcome; and\r\n+- why the work is being done.\r\n+\r\n+Use outcome language. Do not describe activity alone as success.\r\n+\r\n+### 3. Scope\r\n+\r\n+Record:\r\n+\r\n+- included work;\r\n+- explicit exclusions;\r\n+- areas and behaviors that must remain unchanged;\r\n+- existing completed or uncommitted work that must be preserved; and\r\n+- actions that require separate user authority.\r\n+\r\n+Parallelization never broadens this scope.\r\n+\r\n+### 4. Sources of truth\r\n+\r\n+List, in priority order:\r\n+\r\n+- current user instructions;\r\n+- governing specifications and approved `Development_Docs` material;\r\n+- maintained architecture, security, testing, and operational documentation;\r\n+- canonical code and data directories;\r\n+- relevant tests and runtime evidence;\r\n+- external dependencies or authoritative external documentation; and\r\n+- the rule to apply when sources disagree.\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]

Do not finish one before starting the other.\r\n  42: - **Three to five independent lanes:** start every ready lane concurrently whenever capacity allows. Do not hold ready work merely to simplify coordination.\r\n  43: - **Six to twelve independent lanes:** use the full safe ready-lane count immediately when installed capacity permits. Large audits, investigations, cross-system reviews, multi-surface implementations, testing initiatives, and architecture analyses should normally use six to twelve direct workers when they naturally decompose that far. Twelve direct workers are explicitly acceptable, not required.\r\n  44: - **More than twelve independent lanes:** prioritize by dependency, criticality, uncertainty, and value; run waves; and fill each newly available slot immediately rather than waiting for a whole wave to finish.\r\n  45: \r\n  46: Every worker must own a distinct subsystem, package, route group, component family, animation system, evidence source, bug hypothesis, acceptance criterion, test shard, review concern, risk category, document, non-overlapping file set, or verification responsibility. Never create duplicate prompts, duplicate full-repository scans without different purposes, microscopic artificial lanes, overlapping writers, or workers spawned only to reach twelve.\r\n  47: \r\n  48: When a substantial task has materially more ready independent work than active workers, either fill safe capacity or record the concrete reason for under-utilization. \"The coordinator can do it,\" sequential simplicity, prior low worker count, planning effort, or deferring ready work are not sufficient reasons. Unavailable thread capacity, overlapping writes, strict dependency, an exclusive runtime/database/migration/lockfile/generated artifact/browser state, undefined scope, destructive operations, security/authorization boundaries, or high duplication risk are valid reasons.\r\n  49: \r\n  50: ## Progressive fan-out\r\n  51: \r\n  52: Verify the minimum safety baseline first: repository root, applicable instructions, user scope, working-tree state, existing task state, current modifications, exclusive resources, and destructive boundaries. Then launch obvious independent read-only lanes immediately while the coordinator refines the plan. Do not delay safe discovery until every planning table is complete. Do not start write lanes until ownership and integration boundaries are explicit. Add newly discovered ready lanes dynamically, collapse redundant lanes, release unused capacity, and preserve useful partial findings.\r\n  53: \r\n  54: ## Canonical repository context\r\n  55: \r\n  56: - The canonical Git repository is `Kgray44/treasurehuntSoT`; resolve its root dynamically with `git rev-parse --show-toplevel`. `main` is the canonical integrated branch. Do not treat snapshots, compatibility routes, validation copies, or former feature branches as alternate applications.\r\n  59: - Primary implementation locations are `src/app`, `src/components`, `src/animation`, `src/domain`, `src/lib`, `src/platform`, `src/server`, `src/tall-tale`, `prisma`, `public`, and `scripts`.
